<div id="review_199979986" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/199979986" />
    <a title="LemonLinda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1541888-lemonlinda"><img alt="LemonLinda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604612189p2/1541888.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/199979986?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="LemonLinda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="LemonLinda" href="/user/show/1541888-lemonlinda">LemonLinda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/4704796-pope-joan">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer199979986" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11152577221082948174">Cross convinced me that Pope Joan was an actual historical figure who was briliant and compassionate and through her sheer force of will climbed her way up the church hierarchy right in the midst of the Dark Ages to be anointed as Pope. The story began of a brilliant young girl who was first taught to read and write by her older brother much to the chagrin of her abusive father. After attracting the attention of a scholar she is taken with her other brother to a school for advanced study at the </span>
  <span id="freeText11152577221082948174" style="display:none">Cross convinced me that Pope Joan was an actual historical figure who was briliant and compassionate and through her sheer force of will climbed her way up the church hierarchy right in the midst of the Dark Ages to be anointed as Pope. The story began of a brilliant young girl who was first taught to read and write by her older brother much to the chagrin of her abusive father. After attracting the attention of a scholar she is taken with her other brother to a school for advanced study at the request of the bishop which the father cannot refuse. She lives with a handsome knight and his family while at the "schola". The two of them become quite close which becomes a problem. While he is away and after an attack from a band of Norsemen from which she narrowly escapes she assumes the identity of her brother who dies during the attack becoming John instead of Joan. She then enters into the brotherhood of monks at a nearby monastery and distinguishes herself as an accomplished healer, but she also incurs the wrath of the Abbott. So once again she escapes with identity intact and makes her way to Rome. <br /><br />In Rome she quickly established herself as John Anglicus, a priest with a great reputation for healing and is invited to attend to the ailing Pope Sergius. She makes great progress with him where others could not and quickly becomes indispensable to him thus propelling herself on a trajectory to the papal office itself in spite of her gender as no one ever thinks of questioning her gender. They all assume that she is a priest who studied at a monastery in Frankland and is a very talented healer and brilliant reasoner - all things that they believed women to be incapable of achieving. <br /><br />The story brings together history, religious doctrine, romance, intrigue, mystery and a power struggle from the Dark Ages and does so in a well conceived, well researched and well written novel. Loved it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11152577221082948174" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_10682557" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/10682557" />
    <a title="Mary Seay" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/698728-mary-seay"><img alt="Mary Seay" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/10682557?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary Seay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary Seay" href="/user/show/698728-mary-seay">Mary Seay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Unknown Binding 9780704380844" href="/book/show/386699.Pope_Joan">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer10682557" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15061563318900505478">I'll pick this book from my shelf at odd times during the year, and no matter what page I land on I get sucked in all over again. It's an engrossing read, well-researched and well-written, that brings each character to life with stunning clarity. The author crafts the heroine in such a way that her perceptions on the current state of the church are far from the heresy one might worry would pervade this novel. In fact, for me, it reinforced the intelligence and plain-clothes wisdom of Christ that</span>
  <span id="freeText15061563318900505478" style="display:none">I'll pick this book from my shelf at odd times during the year, and no matter what page I land on I get sucked in all over again. It's an engrossing read, well-researched and well-written, that brings each character to life with stunning clarity. The author crafts the heroine in such a way that her perceptions on the current state of the church are far from the heresy one might worry would pervade this novel. In fact, for me, it reinforced the intelligence and plain-clothes wisdom of Christ that the church officials had all but wiped clean from the faith. While I don't think the purpose of this novel is a dissertation on faith, it does make you take a step back and deconstruct the difference between dogma and how God speaks to your heart. It's a glowing testament to the power of one woman's dream to break free from the world's restraints and be recognized for her mind instead of her gender.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15061563318900505478" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2988484734" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2988484734" />
    <a title="Paloma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5931265-paloma"><img alt="Paloma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579496209p2/5931265.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2988484734?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paloma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paloma" href="/user/show/5931265-paloma">Paloma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780307452368" href="/book/show/6216972-pope-joan">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5931265-paloma?shelf=literatura-estadounidense">literatura-estadounidense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5931265-paloma?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5931265-paloma?shelf=reviewed-rese%C3%B1ados">reviewed-reseñados</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5931265-paloma?shelf=novela-hist%C3%B3rica-historical-novel">novela-histórica-historical-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5931265-paloma?shelf=reading-challenge-2019">reading-challenge-2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2988484734" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11945453180260042121"><b>Review in English | Reseña en español (pendiente)</b><br/><br/>An awesome historical novel about a quite interesting character –Pope Joan, the only woman that accessed the Vatican throne. Her existence is part of the many of the black legends surrounding the Catholic Church, as she is denied and was erased from the official history. Nevertheless, the author drew from records and put some pieces together. Whether Joan existed or not, she does seem very real in this historical fiction that recreated her life an</span>
  <span id="freeText11945453180260042121" style="display:none"><b>Review in English | Reseña en español (pendiente)</b><br /><br />An awesome historical novel about a quite interesting character –Pope Joan, the only woman that accessed the Vatican throne. Her existence is part of the many of the black legends surrounding the Catholic Church, as she is denied and was erased from the official history. Nevertheless, the author drew from records and put some pieces together. Whether Joan existed or not, she does seem very real in this historical fiction that recreated her life and doings in the dark ages. <br /><br />Johana is born to a very religious father, who sees her as a burden as she is a girl. Her life is not easy –as mentioned, his father is a very strict man who constantly punishes his wife who she took from the “barbarians” or German people that were conquered. She has two older brothers who her father prefers and she is seen just as someone that should be married off when she becomes of age. But Johana soon becomes interested and passionate about learning and his older brother starts teaching her to read and write. However, tragedy soon strikes –his brother dies and when his father insists that the middle brother, John, is prepared to become a priest, Joan rebels and constantly challenges his father. <br /><br />However, her knowledge surprises one of her tutors, who promises she’ll help her continue her education. When she is ten, she is sent to another town, together with John, were she continues learning but also faces the hatred of other tutors, who see her as an aberration as women were seen inferior to men and incapable of any rational thought. However, she also finds kind people around her, particularly Gerald, who quickly notices her wit and intelligence and takes her under his protection, becoming her longest relationship and a source of support. <br /><br />Years go by and one day, the village where they live is raided by Vikings. Gerald is away, John is killed and Johana makes a decision –she takes on her brother’s identity and enters a monastery as a man. From this point on, she’ll keep her womanhood a secret in order to continue learning and studying as she wishes. Eventually she’ll get to Rome where her skill, wisdom and knowledge will put her on the road to the throne of Saint Peter. She becomes confident of Popes but also gets involved on all the intrigue and ambition in the Vatican. Joan even has crisis as she questions at time the existence of God based on the injustices and crimes she sees. <br /><br />To me, this was a good story, well-built and interesting at all times. The construction of the historical context made me feel completely immersed and the plot had me on my sit at all times. I was particularly surprised and upset by the depiction of the misogyny on those times –true, even today as women we face many injustices and discrimination, but centuries ago it was just too cruel, too unfair for us. Johana is told many times that her desire to learn was unnatural, evil, based on the ideas of men. I felt completely insulted and mad at how men had no difficulty in believing and accepting those ideas and how they humiliated the few women that wanted to learn. I recall one scene, were Johana is already at the monastery, and a rich lady wants to pray at their Church as she has recently lost a baby. That lady, Johana learns, is able to read and write and is quite learned. The other brothers mention that she probably lost her baby as punishment for doing “unwomanly things” and they do not let her enter to pray as 30 days have not yet pass since childbirth and she is still “dirty”. Like, WTF?<br /><br />It is hard to believe that people could have such ignorant ideas, but then again, many of these beliefs remain in our days. Johanna’s story is an exception and she had to give up many things –her identity, her gender, and her mother, and in the end, she lost. <br /><br />Fiction or reality, <i>Pope Joan</i> is a good portrait of the fights women have endured over the centuries and that we must not forget. That said, I did not give it five starts because particularly the last bit seemed to drag in some scenes that were a bit unnecessary and, as one of the reviews point out, in some parts when Johana’s identity was about to be discovered, by a “miracle” it was not. Otherwise it is a very interesting read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11945453180260042121" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('FvuEnS2qm+McUGI0BcldssVR4AXZSw7bnBqa7xv+z9+GypOYvyblt944Fit0iTY0soToYjOLM7+tSPQ/otidNw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

En estas cartas manuscritas relata, con lenguaje íntimo y apasionado, confidencias de su azarosa vida antes de conocerle y su radical transformación tras el encuentro de ambos en Galilea.\n\nNacida en Magdala e hija de un rico comerciante en salazón de pescado, que maltrataba a su madre, todavía adolescente se ve obligada a huir y atravesar duras y arriesgadas situaciones: desde un lupanar en Cesarea Marítima a la humillación de ser vendida como esclava, favorita del rey de los nabateos y famosa bailarina en Tiberíades, pasando por el amor de un centurión romano, la explotación de una banda de beduinos en el desierto y la amistad de un sabio griego y un médico judío. Fascinada por Jesús, que la cura de sus dolencias, se convierte en su más fiel seguidora hasta su muerte y resurrección. \n\nEstas cartas pretenden retratar la psicología de una mujer buscadora, libre y compleja, ante la trágica experiencia de un amor tan espiritualmente grande como humanamente imposible, que la supera y la sublima. Con esta nueva novela, Pedro Miguel Lamet se sirve del intimista género epistolar para relatar en primera persona una singular visión del evangelio desde la óptica de una mujer maltratada y enamorada. Al mismo tiempo pretende, con sus hallazgos y respuestas, ofrecer una liberadora vía de ayuda, consuelo y crecimiento interior a cuantos, desde la soledad, el dolor y la marginación, se enfrentan hoy In the Bible, her life is only hinted at in a brief and violent detour within the more familiar chapters of the Book of Genesis that are about her father, Jacob, and his dozen sons. Told in Dinah\'s voice, this novel reveals the traditions and turmoils of ancient womanhood—the world of the red tent. It begins with the story of her mothers—Leah, Rachel, Zilpah, and Bilhah—the four wives of Jacob. They love Dinah and give her gifts that sustain her through a hard-working youth, a calling to midwifery, and a new home in a foreign land. Dinah\'s story reaches out from a remarkable period of early history and creates an intimate connection with the past. Deeply affecting, The Red Tent combines rich storytelling with a valuable achievement in modern fiction: a new view of biblical women\'s society.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"8782581484185860883\" Buntschatten verhalten sich ruhiger und lassen ihm die Chance, Kontakt mit ihnen aufzunehmen. Fledermäuse hingegen flattern wild um ihn herum, und in ihrer Ge<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText5186462016282259629\" style=\"display:none\">Buntschatten und Fledermäuse, so unterscheidet Axel Brauns die Menschen in seiner Umgebung. Buntschatten verhalten sich ruhiger und lassen ihm die Chance, Kontakt mit ihnen aufzunehmen. Fledermäuse hingegen flattern wild um ihn herum, und in ihrer Gegenwart fühlt er sich nicht wohl. Axel ist Autist und lebt in einer anderen Welt. Sein Buch gewährt uns einen tiefen Einblick in diese abgegrenzte, auf einer eigenen Ordnung beruhenden Welt, in der sich Axel wohl fühlt, die er aber gezwungenermaßen verlassen muss, um in unserer Gesellschaft nicht unter die Räder zu kommen. Im Alter von zwei Jahren bricht die Krankheit aus: Axels Wahrnehmung verblasst, er verliert die Fähigkeit, seine Mitmenschen zu erkennen und zu verstehen, sein Sprachvermögen versiegt. Doch die Eltern kämpfen unermüdlich dagegen an, dass ihr Sohn in der sozialen Isolation versinkt. Mit viel Mühe, Geduld sowie einigen Tricksereien gelingt es, Axel so &quot;normal&quot; wie möglich aufwachsen zu lassen. Er kommt in den Kindergarten, wird eingeschult und wechselt später sogar auf das &quot;Geräusch&quot; -- das Wort &quot;Gymnasium&quot; hat für Axel keinen Klang, und klanglose Worte sind für ihn nur &quot;Geräusche&quot;. Doch trotz der vermittelten Normalität verbringt er die meiste Zeit in seiner Welt, weil dort vieles einfacher ist (&quot;Es gibt Dinge, die man versteht, und es gibt Dinge, die man nicht versteht. Buntschatten gehörten zu den Dingen, die man nicht versteht.&quot;) Axel besteht das Abitur und beginnt ein BWL-Studium. Er hat dem System ein Schnippchen geschlagen: &quot;Die einen bleiben sitzen, die anderen werden versetzt. Ich gehörte zu keiner der beiden Arten, ich hatte es geschafft, bereits vor der ersten Klasse sitzen zu bleiben, ohne dass es ein Lehrer gemerkt hatte.&quot; Trotz seines Arrangements mit der Normalität bleibt eine gewisse Tragik spürbar, denn die Gefühlswelt der Buntschatten bleibt Axel verschlossen. Die Bedeutung von Liebe, Tod, Mitleid und Humor erschließt sich ihm nur ansatzweise. Und dieses Unvermögen macht Axel wohl am meisten zu schaffen, wenn er am Ende bekennt: &quot;Alle Jugendlichen spazierten mit Siebenmeilenstiefeln in das Leben hinaus. Niemals würde ich ihnen folgen können.&quot; Vielleicht gelingt es uns Buntschatten mithilfe dieses bewegenden Buches, Axel Brauns Welt ein bisschen besser zu verstehen. --Christoph Originaria de los reinos cristianos del norte, bella, inteligen<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText14200811589454916685\" style=\"display:none\">Subh Um Walad, la señora, favorita del califa Alhaquén y madre del califa Hixem, fue seguramente el personaje más singular y apasionante del esplendoroso período del Califato de Córdoba. Originaria de los reinos cristianos del norte, bella, inteligente y cultivada, tuvo que vivir la realidad de palacio, sometida al régimen propio del harén, junto a las concubinas y los eunucos. Pero se rebeló contra este destino y se convirtió en alguien determinante dentro del complejo ambiente familiar de la realeza omeya que residía por entonces en Medina Azahara.Cuando a finales del primer milenio, Abuámir Almansur se halla en lo más alto de su poder y se lanza a su enérgica campaña final para conquistar todo el Norte y destruir definitivamente los reinos cristianos, el invulnerable personaje ignora que a sus espaldas se está fraguando una conspiración que intentará torcer el rumbo de la Historia…Subh Um Walad, la señora, decide romper definitivamente con su encierro en los Alcázares y regresa a Medina Azahara, la ciudad de los califas, para liderar junto a su hermano Eneko un heterogéneo grupo formado por curiosos personajes, pero nada es lo que parece y todo se confunde en aquella metrópoli única y luminosa a la vez que delirante. Es una época de exuberancia creadora y brillantez intelectual en Alándalus, y los poetas como el joven Farid, originario de Alejandría, son protagonistas de excepción que saben aprovechar su talento para estar cerca de los poderosos.Jesús Sánchez Adalid regresa a los escenarios de la Córdoba cercana al año 1000 y a la fascinadora Medina Azahara, que pugna por seguir siendo baluarte califal frente a la ambiciones del caudillo Almansur.Conspiraciones, enredos y poesía, la vida de la mujer más poderosa de la Córdoba califal. Los baños del pozo azul es una &quot;reivindicación del mundo femenino en una época en que la historia lo ha ocultado&quot;. \n  El País\nJesús Sánchez Adalid publica &quot;Los baños del pozo Azul&quot;, una novela histórica que se adentra en la figura histórica de Subh Umm Walad. Un libro que, además de desvelar a un personaje oculto en las páginas del pasado, ayuda a destruir mitos como el que afirma que cristianos y musulmanes no se relacionaban entre ellos. &quot;Sus mundos no eran dos compartimentos estancos&quot;, completa.\n  ABC\nEl papel decisivo de diversas mujeres, como la favorita Subh, hará que de nuevo cerremos una novela de Jesús Sánchez Adalid con una sensación de sosiego por habernos reencontrado con la Historia.\n  Anika entre libros\nJesús Sánchez Adalid es, hoy en día, uno de los referentes de novela histórica en este país y ya me ganó con &quot;El mozárabe&quot;. &quot;Los baños del Pozo Azul&quot; es una ambiciosa novela con un riguroso trasfondo histórico, de ritmo desigual y leves dosis de misterio al incluirse una serie de desconcertantes muertes en su argumento.\n  Mis Lecturas\n&quot;Sánchez Adalid tiene el don de narrar de forma pausada y reflexiva. Literariamente deudora de la elegancia de la mejor novela clásica.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/44605.Donna_Woolfolk_Cross">About Donna Woolfolk Cross</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12571264383863808961">Donna Woolfolk Cross graduated cum laude, Phi Beta Kappa, from the University of Pennsylvania in 1969 with a B.A. in English. She moved to London, England, after graduation, and worked as an editorial assistant for a small publishing house on Fleet Street, W.H. Allen and Company. Upon her return to the United States, Cross worked at Young and Rubicam, a Madison Avenue advertising firm, before goin</span>
  <span id="freeText12571264383863808961" style="display:none">Donna Woolfolk Cross graduated cum laude, Phi Beta Kappa, from the University of Pennsylvania in 1969 with a B.A. in English. She moved to London, England, after graduation, and worked as an editorial assistant for a small publishing house on Fleet Street, W.H. Allen and Company. Upon her return to the United States, Cross worked at Young and Rubicam, a Madison Avenue advertising firm, before going on to graduate school at UCLA where she earned a master's degree in Literature and Writing in 1972.<br /><br />In 1973, Cross moved with her husband to upstate New York where she began teaching writing in a college English Department. Now writing is her fulltime career.<br /><br />She is the author of two books on language, Word Abuse: How the Words We Use Use Us and Mediaspeak: How Television Makes Up Your Mind. She is the coauthor of Speaking of Words and Daddy's Little Girl. The product of seven years of research and writing, Pope Joan is her first novel. She is now at work on a new novel set in 17th century France.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12571264383863808961" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
